    (全班暂停了讲授，安静地查阅了模块摘要，阅读了教学大纲，并在讲座恢复前做好了准备。)

  - [18:31:05 - 18:36:08] **Workload Expectations and Types of Intelligence**

    Okay, that's good. Thirty-five minutes have already passed. I think many of you are spot on regarding what I will cover, but some of you are a little off track. Let's see if I cover the outline of the module accurately, and then you can decide by the end of the day if you still want to take this module or if you want to drop it. A smaller class size is always nice for the lecturers as well! For those who are new to me—I know a bunch of you are already familiar faces—you can call me either Anna or Purnima, either way is fine. I have been associated with NUS since 2003, which is a long time now, and I have been teaching in this department since 2000. I actually started teaching when I was still a PhD student, so it has been quite many years. I have been officially lecturing since around 2007 or 2008. As I shared with a few of you at the beginning of the class, MT5010 is an elective module. You do not strictly need to be here. MT5007 is a core module that you must complete, but this one is by choice. That is why I will do my due diligence to chase you away today! If you choose to stay, it means I hope you have a genuine interest in the subject because this is a very labor-intensive module. I have reduced the workload tremendously compared to past iterations, but if you are going to accurately look at the future, you still need to read tons and tons of material. Reading doesn't mean you have to memorize and imbibe every single detail. You need to give it a cursory look, grasp the bigger picture, and identify the important aspects. You note down what is relevant, and only later on will you dive deep into the specific techniques. If you look at forecasting, which many of you mentioned, there are dozens of tools, techniques, and analyses available. No single module can do justice to teaching you every single one perfectly. My goal here is to expose you to the breadth of different techniques and explain their advantages and disadvantages. For example, I will cover both qualitative and quantitative techniques, giving you a solid idea of how a few key qualitative ones are executed. The reason for this approach is that when you are expected to apply foresighting in the real world, you have to dive deep into the specific technique best suited for your scenario, as not all techniques work for every situation. You will build up that specific knowledge along the way. As an intelligence or foresighting officer, you need to read mountains of boring, drowsy documents. Trust me, I will intentionally assign at least a couple of articles that will put you straight to sleep. When I first prepared this module, I had to re-read some articles three or four times because I kept dozing off! But that is exactly the dirty job of an intelligence officer. You need to look for what is called "grey information" and explore the "white spaces." To find those hidden gems that bring value to your organization, you have to dig through dry reports. If you only look at obvious clues, like reading the news to see what is happening in the industry, you are already too late. By the time it is published as a news article, your competitors have already seen it, and you will not win the race. The smartness lies in becoming the news article before the news is even written. To do that, we classify information into three types: white, grey, and black. White information is publicly available, published data—things like news articles, patents, academic publications, and commercialized products. Grey information is data you actively collect by talking directly to experts. It requires hand-collecting intelligence by asking them where they see the industry five years down the line. Many foresighting articles are actually the outcome of these expert interviews. Then, there is something called black information. I asked the class what they thought black information was, comparing it to "black money."

    好的，非常好。已经过去三十五分钟了。我认为你们中的很多人对我要讲的内容猜得很准，但也有一些人有点偏离轨道。让我们看看我接下来对课程大纲的介绍，到今天结束时，你们可以决定是继续修这门课，还是退课。对于讲师来说，小班授课总是件好事！对于那些还不认识我的人——我知道你们中有一部分已经是熟面孔了——你们可以叫我Anna，或者Purnima，怎么叫都行。我从2003年起就与新加坡国立大学结缘，到现在已经很久了，而且我从2000年就开始在系里教书。其实我还在读博士的时候就开始教书了，所以已经有很多年了。大约从2007年、2008年开始，我就一直在主讲课程。正如我在课前和你们几个人分享的那样，MT5010是一门选修课。你们并非非得坐在这里。MT5007是必修课，你们必须完成，但这门是选修课。这就是为什么我今天会尽职尽责地“赶”你们走！如果你们选择留下来，我希望你们对这门课有真正的兴趣，因为这是一门工作量非常大的课。与过去的版本相比，我已经大幅减少了工作量，但如果你们想准确地预测未来，仍然需要阅读成吨成吨的材料。阅读并不意味着你必须记住和吸收每一个细节。你需要粗略地浏览，掌握大局，并找出重要的方面。你把相关的部分记下来，只有在以后你才会深入研究具体的技术。如果你去了解很多人提到的“预测”（forecasting），你会发现有几十种可用的工具、技术和分析方法。没有任何一门课程能完美地教会你所有的方法。我在这里的目标是让你们接触到各种不同的技术，并解释它们的优缺点。例如，我将涵盖定性和定量两种技术，让你们对如何执行几个关键的定性方法有一个扎实的了解。这种方法的原因在于，当你需要在现实世界中应用预见技术时，你必须深入研究最适合你具体场景的技术，因为并不是所有的技术都适用于所有情况。你会在此过程中积累具体的知识。作为一名情报或预见官员，你需要阅读堆积如山、枯燥乏味、让人昏昏欲睡的文件。相信我，我会故意布置至少几篇能让你直接睡着的文章。当我第一次准备这门课时，有些文章我不得不重读三四遍，因为我总是读着读着就打瞌睡了！但这正是情报官员必须要做的苦差事。你需要寻找所谓的“灰色信息”，并探索“空白领域”。为了找到那些能给你的组织带来价值的隐藏瑰宝，你必须在枯燥的报告中深挖。如果你只关注明显的线索，比如通过看新闻来了解行业动态，那你就已经太迟了。当它作为新闻报道发表时，你的竞争对手也已经看到了，你就无法赢得比赛。真正的聪明之处在于，在新闻被写出来之前，你就成为了新闻报道的主角。为了做到这一点，我们将信息分为三种类型：白色、灰色和黑色。白色信息是公开可用的、已发布的数据——比如新闻文章、专利、学术出版物和商业化产品。灰色信息是你通过直接与专家交谈主动收集的数据。这需要通过询问他们对未来五年行业的看法来手工收集情报。许多关于预见的文章实际上就是这些专家访谈的结果。然后，还有一种叫做黑色信息。我问全班同学他们认为黑色信息是什么，并把它比作“黑钱”。

  - [18:36:08 - 18:38:13] **Black Information and Dirty Operations**

    Just like "dirty money," black information essentially refers to "dirty information." I asked the class how one might obtain it. A student correctly suggested insider trading, which is certainly one possible way. To give you another example, in some highly competitive industries—especially the pharmaceutical sector, which I might have mentioned to my MT5007 students before—companies will literally send people to look into the trash cans of their competitors. They do this because there could be absolute wealth hidden in that trash. The competitor shreds their documents and throws them out, and the other company digs in, pieces it together, and extracts valuable intelligence from it. Another common tactic, which happens very frequently in big tech companies, is hijacking key personnel from one firm to another to extract proprietary knowledge. All of these tactics fall under the umbrella of black information. Now, if you want to be at the absolute forefront of innovation, please do not go around telling people that your NUS professor is propagating illegal activities! I am not endorsing this; I am simply explaining the reality of what actually happens out there in the industry. The truth is, if you want to lead in innovation, people will look for all kinds of information through any means necessary. You absolutely cannot afford to just sit back, wait for a neatly published white paper, and then use that to make your strategic company decisions. That approach simply will not work. So, in the process of teaching you how nasty and cutthroat the real world of technology intelligence is, I will also make you read some nasty, complex articles. If you feel you are not ready for that kind of rigorous, uncomfortable analysis, it is genuinely fine with me if you drop the module.

    就像“黑钱”一样，黑色信息本质上指的是“肮脏的信息”。我问全班同学怎样才能获得这种信息。一位学生准确地指出了内幕交易，这当然是可能的一种方式。再给你们举个例子，在一些竞争极其激烈的行业——尤其是制药行业，我以前可能和MT5007的学生提到过——公司真的会派人去翻竞争对手的垃圾桶。他们这样做是因为那里面可能隐藏着绝对的财富。竞争对手将文件粉碎并扔掉，而另一家公司则去挖掘、拼凑，并从中提取有价值的情报。另一种常见的策略，在大型科技公司中经常发生，就是从一家公司挖走关键人员到另一家公司，以获取专有知识。所有这些策略都属于黑色信息的范畴。现在，如果你想站在创新的绝对前沿，请不要到处跟人说你们的新加坡国立大学教授在宣传非法活动！我并不是在鼓励这种行为；我只是在解释行业中实际发生的现实情况。事实是，如果你想在创新方面保持领先，人们会通过任何必要的手段寻找各种信息。你绝对不能只是袖手旁观，等待一份排版精美的白皮书发表，然后用它来制定你的公司战略决策。这种方法根本行不通。因此，在教导你们现实世界中的技术情报是多么残酷无情的同时，我也会让你们阅读一些艰深、复杂的文章。如果你觉得自己还没准备好进行这种严谨而令人不适的分析，如果你退选这门课，我是完全可以接受的。

  - [18:38:13 - 18:41:20] **Visual Summaries for Decision Makers**

    The second major thing you must understand for this module is how to communicate your findings. As decision makers, bosses are severely time-pressed. They are simply not going to read your 10-page or 20-page intelligence report. Whatever intelligence you gather, you must be able to summarize it beautifully and concisely in a neat pictorial form. For example, look at this Big Data Analytics map provided in your slides. This framework represents months and months of grueling research efforts. Yet, it distills all that work into clear blocks. In one glance, it tells the decision makers exactly who the key players are—companies they know, companies they don't know, the core technologies currently in play, and the specific departments and agencies they need to tap into for R&D funding and environment support.

    As an intelligence officer, every outcome you produce must be presented in a concise, pictorial form like this. When your bosses give it a cursory look, they instantly get the bigger picture. If they find an area interesting and want to dive deeper, they will ask you, and only then will you hand over the hundreds of pages of supporting documents. But your initial presentation must be visual. Therefore, many of the assignments and presentations you will do for this module will not be long, written essays going "blah, blah, blah." Instead, they will be in the form of mind maps, roadmaps, or whatever creative pictorial formats you can think of. This is meant to train you to be a highly effective analyst. You can easily generate written text now using ChatGPT and other tools, but your true value lies in how you present and structure that information visually. I will assign homework where you have to read a very boring article, extract the core gist, and present it visually. This will test whether you are actually capable of picking the hidden gems out of a pile of rubbish and serving it in a format that is palatable to a time-pressed executive. Does that make sense? Again, if you feel you are not up to this task, please drop the module. So, expect heavy reading, expect to create visual presentations, and be prepared to engage in forum discussions. Also, just so you know, I do not take physical attendance for this module, unlike MT5007, and I will make the webcasts available for you to review.

    关于这门课，你们必须了解的第二件大事是如何传达你们的发现。作为决策者，老板们的时间非常紧迫。他们根本不会去读你那长达10页或20页的情报报告。无论你收集到什么情报，你都必须能够以简洁清晰的图表形式将其完美地总结出来。例如，看看你们幻灯片中提供的大数据分析图。这个框架代表了数月艰苦的研究成果。然而，它将所有这些工作提炼成了清晰的区块。一眼看去，它就能准确地告诉决策者主要的参与者是谁——他们认识的公司、他们不认识的公司、目前正在发挥作用的核心技术，以及他们需要利用哪些特定的部门和机构来获得研发资金和环境支持。

    作为一名情报官员，你产出的每一个成果都必须像这样以简洁的图表形式呈现。当你的老板们粗略地看一眼时，他们立刻就能掌握大局。如果他们对某个领域感兴趣并想深入了解，他们会问你，只有在那时，你才会递交数百页的支持文件。但你最初的汇报必须是可视化的。因此，你们这门课要做的许多作业和演讲都不会是长篇大论、满篇“废话”的文字。相反，它们将以思维导图、路线图或你能想到的任何创造性的图表形式呈现。这是为了训练你们成为一名高效的分析师。你们现在可以很容易地使用ChatGPT和其他工具生成文本，但你们的真正价值在于如何直观地呈现和构建这些信息。我会布置作业，要求你们阅读一篇非常无聊的文章，提取核心要点，并将其可视化地呈现出来。这将考验你们是否真的有能力从一堆垃圾中挑出隐藏的宝石，并以时间紧迫的高管能够接受的格式提供给他们。这说得通吗？重申一次，如果你觉得自己无法胜任这项任务，请退选这门课。所以，做好大量阅读的准备，做好制作可视化演示的准备，并准备好参与论坛讨论。另外，顺便说一下，与MT5007不同，这门课我不点名，我也会提供课程的在线录像供你们复习。

  - [18:41:20 - 18:46:07] **Grading Breakdown and Forum Rules**

    We have a sizable number of students here today, though not everyone has arrived yet. If you are expected to read an article for the week, please actually read it because we rely heavily on class discussions. I will not be spoon-feeding the content of the papers during the lecture; we need to rush through the core concepts. The grading for this module is structured into two parts: an individual component worth 60% and a group component worth 40%. The group component is a major project centered around technology intelligence activities in a company like Straumann. The individual component is split evenly: 30% for class participation and 30% for a logbook due by April 26th. For those who took MT5007, you already know what a logbook entails. For those who haven't, let me explain. A logbook is basically a structured reflection journal. For example, the core topic this week is "What is intelligence and foresighting?" You will maintain a logbook of what we cover. There are three levels of reflection in a logbook. Level One is simply recording the concepts: "What is intelligence? What is foresighting?"—basically summarizing our class discussion. Level Two is relating those academic concepts to your own personal examples, workplace situations, or life experiences. You would write, "I engaged in this kind of foresighting at my job, and this is how we did it." Level Three requires deeper critical thinking. It involves documenting an intelligence or foresighting activity you attempted, the specific problems or roadblocks you encountered, and the valuable lessons you extracted from that failure or struggle that would be informative to others. It is about questioning the frameworks and analyzing the friction points. You are required to maintain this logbook for five different weekly topics. It could be Weeks 1 to 5, allowing you to finish the requirement entirely before the midterm break, or you can pick topics from the second half of the module where we cover more hands-on analytical tools.

    Now, regarding the 30% for class participation, you can earn this by throwing your ideas into our live classroom discussions, which my TA Cheng Hong will note down. You can also earn participation marks by contributing to the Canvas forum, similar to MT5007. However, last year I received feedback that some students were just copying and pasting from ChatGPT into the forum just to artificially inflate their participation numbers. I knew they were doing it, and it frustrated the students who were taking the time to write out thoughtful contributions based on their actual professional experiences. To fix this, I have decided to split the forum discussions into two distinct categories this semester. One thread will explicitly allow the use of ChatGPT. I know some of you are students without deep industry work experience, and I do not want to put you at a disadvantage. If you use ChatGPT, that is fine, but learn something from the prompt output and post a synthesized thought, do not just blindly copy-paste long essays. I am strictly capping those ChatGPT-assisted posts to no more than 100 words—keep it short. Then, I am going to open a completely separate thread exclusively for those who are NOT using ChatGPT, where the discussion must be entirely rooted in real-world, personal experience. As a student named Litiyant accurately pointed out during class, a post grounded in rich, real-world experience naturally holds more value than a generic AI-generated response. While everyone can still read and learn from both threads, I want to ensure that the professionals sharing genuine, experiential insights are not drowned out or bombarded by a flood of ChatGPT messages. I hope that even the students using AI will absorb some knowledge through the process of prompting and searching. Cheng Hong and I will carefully track live class participation based on quality, and I will moderate the forums, occasionally pulling interesting forum threads to discuss live in the following week's class.

    今天我们在座的学生人数不少，虽然不是所有人都到了。如果要求你们本周阅读一篇文章，请务必真正去读，因为我们非常依赖课堂讨论。我不会在课上把论文的内容嚼碎了喂给你们；我们需要快速过一遍核心概念。这门课的评分分为两部分：个人部分占60%，小组部分占40%。小组部分是一个主要项目，围绕士卓曼（Straumann）等公司的技术情报活动展开。个人部分平分：30%是课堂参与，30%是4月26日交的日志（logbook）。对于上过MT5007的同学来说，你们已经知道日志是什么了。对于没上过的同学，我来解释一下。日志基本上就是一个结构化的反思日记。例如，本周的核心主题是“什么是情报和预见？”你们需要记录我们涵盖的内容。日志的反思分为三个层次。第一层仅仅是记录概念：“什么是情报？什么是预见？”——基本上就是总结我们的课堂讨论。第二层是将这些学术概念与你自己的个人案例、工作场所情况或生活经历联系起来。你会写道：“我在工作中参与了这种预见，我们是这样做的。”第三层需要更深入的批判性思维。它包括记录你尝试过的一项情报或预见活动，你遇到的具体问题或障碍，以及你从失败或挣扎中提取的、对他人有启发意义的宝贵教训。它是关于对框架提出质疑并分析摩擦点。你需要针对五个不同的每周主题维护这个日志。你可以选择第1到第5周，让你在期中休息前完全完成这项要求，或者你也可以从模块的下半部分选择主题，那里我们会涵盖更多动手操作的分析工具。

    现在，关于占30%的课堂参与度，你可以通过在我们的现场课堂讨论中提出你的想法来获得，我的助教正宏（Cheng Hong）会记录下来。你也可以像MT5007一样，通过在Canvas论坛上发言来获得参与分。然而，去年我收到反馈说，有些学生只是把ChatGPT的内容复制粘贴到论坛上，仅仅是为了人为地增加他们的参与次数。我知道他们在这么做，这让那些花时间根据自己的实际专业经验写出有思想深度的帖子的学生感到很沮丧。为了解决这个问题，我决定本学期将论坛讨论分成两个截然不同的类别。一个主题帖将明确允许使用ChatGPT。我知道你们中有些学生没有深厚的行业工作经验，我不想让你们处于劣势。如果你使用ChatGPT，那没问题，但要从提示输出中学到一些东西，并发布一个综合的想法，不要只是盲目地复制粘贴长篇大论。我严格限制那些使用ChatGPT辅助的帖子不得超过100个词——尽量简短。然后，我将专门为那些不使用ChatGPT的人开设一个完全独立的主题帖，那里的讨论必须完全植根于真实的个人经验。正如一位名叫Litiyant的同学在课堂上准确指出的那样，基于丰富的真实世界经验的帖子自然比普通的AI生成的回复更有价值。虽然每个人仍然可以阅读和学习这两个主题帖，但我想确保分享真实的经验见解的专业人士不会被大量的ChatGPT信息淹没或轰炸。我希望即使是使用AI的学生也能通过提示和搜索的过程吸收一些知识。正宏和我将仔细跟踪基于质量的现场课堂参与情况，我将管理论坛，偶尔会提取有趣的论坛主题帖在下周的课堂上进行现场讨论。

  - [18:46:07 - 18:51:39] **The Challenge for the Day: Definitions**

    Are there any questions on the grading so far? Moving on, what I am going to do in every class is post a specific "Challenge for the Day." If the challenge is answered by someone to my absolute satisfaction, that person is completely free to pack up and go home early. I will instantly assume your logbook for that week is perfectly maintained, and I will award you full marks for that week's class participation. Is that clear? If you are up to the challenge, and you nail the answer, you get a free day with full marks. Of course, you are most welcome to stay and listen, but you are free to leave if you win. So, today's challenge is this: What is foresighting, and exactly how is it different from forecasting and intelligence? One of you earlier mentioned that the module title interested you. Here it is: Forecasting, Intelligence, Foresighting. What is the fundamental difference between the three?

    It would help immensely if you all had physical name boards in front of you so I could call out your names. From next class onwards, please bring a piece of paper, write your name on it boldly, and prop it up. It makes it much easier for me to be familiar with you and for Cheng Hong to record your participation accurately. A student named Leitian gave it the first shot. He argued that foresighting relies more on personal experiences and qualitative feelings, whereas forecasting and intelligence use hard data and practical theoretical models. I corrected him, stating that this is not exactly right. You absolutely must use experience and intuition for all three, but more importantly, everything is deeply data-based. You use raw data for forecasting, you use current data for intelligence, and you certainly use data models for foresighting. Another student then proposed that foresighting is about what we would *like* to happen, forecasting is a structured anticipation of what *is* to come, and intelligence is understanding our current position based on information we have right now. I told him he was almost there—he could go for half the class! Another student confidently stated that forecasting is fundamentally looking backwards to predict the future. I agreed enthusiastically; forecasting is indeed about looking backward. A fourth student refined the previous answers, stating that intelligence is based entirely on existing current data to form an opinion, while forecasting is predicting the future timeline based on extrapolating that historical data. I commended him, noting his answer was a highly refined version of the others, scoring about 90% accuracy.

    到目前为止，对评分还有什么问题吗？接下来，我将在每节课提出一个具体的“今日挑战”。如果有人能做出让我完全满意的回答，那个人就可以完全自由地收拾书包提早回家。我会立刻假定你那周的日志已经完美完成，并且我会给你那周的课堂参与打满分。清楚了吗？如果你敢于接受挑战，并且给出了完美的答案，你就可以获得一天的休息时间和满分。当然，我们非常欢迎你留下来旁听，但如果你赢了，你就可以自由离开。所以，今天的挑战是：什么是预见？它与预测和情报到底有什么不同？你们中有人早些时候提到，模块的名称让你们很感兴趣。就是这个：预测（Forecasting）、情报（Intelligence）、预见（Foresighting）。这三者之间的根本区别是什么？

    如果你们面前都有实体的名牌，让我可以叫出你们的名字，那会有很大的帮助。从下节课开始，请带一张纸，把你的名字粗体写在上面，并把它立起来。这会让我更容易熟悉你们，也更容易让正宏准确地记录你们的课堂参与情况。一位名叫Leitian的学生最先尝试回答。他认为，预见更多地依赖于个人经验和定性感受，而预测和情报则使用硬数据和实用的理论模型。我纠正了他，指出这并不完全正确。你绝对必须在所有这三个方面运用经验和直觉，但更重要的是，一切都深深地基于数据。你在预测时使用原始数据，在情报时使用当前数据，在预见时当然也会使用数据模型。另一位学生接着提出，预见是关于我们“希望”发生什么，预测是对将要发生的事情进行结构化的预期，而情报是基于我们现有的信息了解我们目前的状况。我告诉他，他差不多答对了——他可以休息半节课了！另一位学生自信地指出，预测从根本上说是向后看以预测未来。我热情地表示同意；预测确实是向后看的。第四个学生对前面的答案进行了提炼，他说情报完全基于现有的当前数据形成观点，而预测则是基于推断历史数据来预测未来的时间表。我表扬了他，指出他的答案是其他人答案的精炼版本，准确率大约达到了90%。

  - [18:51:39 - 18:57:04] **Hindsight, Insight, and Foresight**

    Since the class successfully pieced the definitions together, I explained that those who answered well could leave if they wished. Let me formally break down the concepts: It all comes down to Hindsight, Insight, and Foresight. Forecasting relies purely on hindsight. You look at the past, gather whatever historical data points you have accumulated, and simply extrapolate that line to predict what the potential future will be one or two periods ahead. Intelligence, on the other hand, is all about generating insights from the absolute present. You are looking at the current trend. For example, when COVID suddenly hit, that was a massive influx of immediate information. An intelligence-driven company acts on that present data immediately. They might realize, "I am in the service sector, my foot traffic is dropping to zero, I need to instantly revamp my operations into digital deliveries." That is taking current intelligence, processing it, and making an agile decision.

    Foresight, however, is deeply futuristic—we are talking five or ten years down the line. I want you to bear in mind, especially those who shared why they took this class: foresighting is *not* about arrogantly predicting exactly what the future will be. If you try to predict a single, rigid future, you are doing foresighting wrong. When looking five to ten years ahead, the future could branch out like this, or like this, or like this. You must paint multiple, completely different potential scenarios of the future. The core value of foresighting is deciding what actions you need to take *today* so that, regardless of which of those painted futures actually becomes reality, you are prepared to navigate through it rather than being blindsided and thrown out of business.

    Let's break this down into a simple personal life example. If I ask a student—let's use Karishma as an example—what her day tomorrow is going to look like, she can easily forecast it: she will wake up, do her day job, and come to her next evening module. But if I ask her to pinpoint exactly what she will be doing months from now, say, on June 15th during the summer, it becomes complicated. Her mother might have plans to travel to India, while her father is lobbying for a trip to Europe. Foresighting is asking: "If the India trip happens, how do I prepare my schedule today? If the Europe trip happens, what do I need to budget now? What if I decide to stay and look for local internships instead?" Foresighting maps out all those potential states and prepares her for whichever one actually materializes.

    Crucially, mapping these multiple futures is still heavily data-based. You must collect diverse datasets to build these scenarios. For instance, if you are painting future job market scenarios, you might analyze which global economies are strengthening, or you might closely track what President Donald Trump is doing regarding immigration and tariffs so you can actively avoid problematic sectors and look elsewhere. You collect data to determine if a technology like AI is a fleeting fad or a permanent disruption. A student earlier mentioned solar energy; you must collect data to determine if solar is still the ultimate path forward or if it is rapidly saturating, requiring you to pivot to alternative energy investments. Everything is rooted in data. Just like intelligence is data-based—for instance, when I entered this classroom, it was freezing cold. Over time, as more human bodies filled the seats, the temperature slowly rose. The raw data is the fluctuating temperature. My brain processing that data—realizing it is getting warmer and deciding whether or not to take off my jacket—is real-time intelligence. This continuous processing of data and experience brings us to Knowledge Management, which is a vital, integral pillar of technology intelligence. I used to teach a whole, dedicated module just on knowledge management, but since I do not have that luxury here, I have dedicated Week 7 specifically to teaching you its most critical aspects.

    既然全班同学成功地把定义拼凑了起来，我解释说，回答得好的同学如果愿意的话可以离开了。让我正式地分解这些概念：这一切都归结为后见之明（Hindsight）、洞察力（Insight）和远见（Foresight）。预测纯粹依赖于后见之明。你回顾过去，收集你所积累的任何历史数据点，然后简单地推断那条线，以预测未来一两个时期的潜在情况。另一方面，情报完全是关于从绝对的现在产生洞察力。你关注的是当前的趋势。例如，当新冠疫情突然爆发时，那是大量即时信息的涌入。一家受情报驱动的公司会立即根据这些当前数据采取行动。他们可能会意识到：“我身处服务业，我的客流量正降至零，我需要立即将我的业务彻底转变为数字化交付。”这就是获取当前情报、对其进行处理并做出敏捷的决策。

    然而，远见（预见）是非常具有未来感的一—我们谈论的是五年或十年后的事情。我希望你们记住，尤其是那些分享了为什么上这门课的同学：预见绝对不是傲慢地准确预测未来会是什么样子。如果你试图预测一个单一的、僵化的未来，那你的预见方法就错了。在展望五到十年后时，未来可能会像这样发展，或者像那样，或者像另一种样子。你必须描绘出多个完全不同的潜在未来情景。预见的核心价值在于决定你“今天”需要采取什么行动，以便无论这些描绘的未来中哪一个真正成为现实，你都做好了应对的准备，而不是措手不及，被淘汰出局。

    让我们把这个分解成一个简单的个人生活例子。如果我问一个学生——让我们以Karishma为例——她明天的一天会是什么样子，她很容易就能预测出来：她会起床，做她的日常工作，晚上来上下一门课。但如果我让她准确指出几个月后，比如在6月15日的夏天，她到底在做什么，事情就变得复杂了。她母亲可能计划去印度旅行，而她父亲则在游说去欧洲旅行。预见就是问：“如果印度之旅成行，我今天该如何准备我的日程安排？如果欧洲之旅成行，我现在需要做多少预算？如果我决定留下来寻找当地的实习机会怎么办？”预见描绘了所有这些潜在的状态，并让她为实际发生的任何一种状态做好准备。

    至关重要的是，描绘这些多重未来仍然严重依赖于数据。你必须收集不同的数据集来构建这些情景。例如，如果你在描绘未来的就业市场情景，你可能会分析哪些全球经济体正在走强，或者你可能会密切关注唐纳德·特朗普总统在移民和关税方面的举措，以便你可以主动避开有问题的部门，将目光投向其他地方。你收集数据来确定像AI这样的技术是转瞬即逝的狂热，还是永久性的颠覆。早些时候有学生提到了太阳能；你必须收集数据来确定太阳能是否仍然是最终的前进道路，或者它是否正在迅速饱和，需要你转向替代能源投资。一切都植根于数据。就像情报是基于数据的一样——例如，当我走进这间教室时，里面冷得要命。随着时间的推移，座位上坐满了人，温度慢慢升高了。原始数据是波动的温度。我的大脑处理这些数据——意识到天气越来越暖和，并决定是否脱掉夹克——这就是实时的情报。这种对数据和经验的持续处理将我们引向了知识管理（Knowledge Management），这是技术情报的一个至关重要、不可或缺的支柱。我曾经专门教过一整门关于知识管理的课程，但由于我在这里没有那个条件，我已经把第7周专门用来教授你们其最关键的方面。

  - [18:57:04 - 19:02:50] **Moving Beyond Reactive Strategies and Levels of Foresight**

    Now you deeply understand the fundamental difference. In earlier eras, businesses only ever talked about forecasting. They took their historical sales data and comfortably extrapolated one or two years into the future. That rudimentary forecasting was perfectly fine back then because technological innovation and environmental shifts were simply not moving at the dramatic, breakneck speeds we see today. As markets sped up, top-notch, innovative companies shifted to Intelligence. They realized that they needed to aggressively monitor clues and instantly change their business models and customer approaches. For example, there was a time in the retail sector when managers rigidly forecasted: "The festive season, like Chinese New Year, is coming; therefore, we must stock up all our products to the maximum because there will be huge guaranteed sales." But over time, utilizing intelligence, they realized that a festive season does not automatically equal massive sales. It is heavily dependent on the surrounding socio-economic context and the consumer's psychological mindset. If the broader economy is unstable and people are terrified about losing their jobs, they are simply not going to spend lavishly, even if it is Chinese New Year. Recognizing this, companies used real-time intelligence to become agile and reactive.

    However, to truly dominate the forefront of innovation today, being highly reactive is still not enough. You cannot constantly run your business by saying, "Oh, a crisis happened today, I will react. A competitor launched a product today, I will react." If you operate that way, you are letting external forces drive you. Foresighting allows you to be the driver of your own destiny. You actively visualize potential futures and take preventative, strategic decisions today so that you are never completely blindsided or thrown out of the industry entirely. A student named Moment asked an excellent question: Do we look at what general technologies will shape the future, or do we focus deeply on how a *particular* technology, like his specific interest in the dropping prices of solar energy, will evolve? I explained that foresighting operates at multiple, distinct levels, which is clearly mapped out in the Lockwood Carlson article you read.

    If you are an R&D manager actively investing capital into solar, wind, or geothermal, your foresighting is highly focused. You analyze if your long-term bet on solar is still sound, or if a competitor's emerging technology dictates that you should pivot your investments. That represents foresighting at the level of a single business group or specific technology. But foresighting scales upwards. It can encompass a whole company, an entire industry, a national government, or even the world. For instance, looking at the country level, the Singaporean government executed the Industry Transformation Maps several years ago. They meticulously evaluated which sectors the national budget should bet its R&D funding on to secure future economic survival. In fact, the National Research Foundation (NRF) is currently highly interested in training their civil servants to be more futuristic in their policy-making, and this very module is part of that effort to determine what the country should bet on. When our guest speaker, Mr. Koo Seng Meng, visits next week, he will discuss his prior work with the NRF, where he applied these foresighting principles at a massive, national level across various sectors. The tools you learn here scale perfectly from personal career planning all the way up to national strategy.

    现在你们深刻理解了根本区别。在早期阶段，企业只谈论预测。他们利用历史销售数据，轻松地推断未来一两年的情况。这种粗略的预测在当时是完全可行的，因为技术创新和环境变化的发生速度根本不像我们今天看到的那么惊人、那么快。随着市场步伐的加快，顶尖的创新型公司转向了情报领域。他们意识到他们需要积极地监控线索，并立即改变他们的商业模式和客户策略。例如，零售业曾经有一个时期，经理们死板地预测：“像农历新年这样的节日快到了；因此，我们必须最大限度地囤积所有的产品，因为肯定会有巨大的销售额。”但随着时间的推移，通过利用情报，他们意识到节日并不自动等同于巨大的销售额。它在很大程度上取决于周围的社会经济环境和消费者的心理状态。如果大环境不稳定，人们非常害怕失去工作，即使是农历新年，他们也绝对不会大肆挥霍。认识到这一点后，公司开始使用实时情报变得敏捷并做出反应。

    然而，要在当今真正主导创新的最前沿，仅仅做到高度敏捷地反应是不够的。你不能总是这样经营企业：“哦，今天发生危机了，我要做出反应。竞争对手今天发布了产品，我要做出反应。”如果你这样运作，你就是在让外部力量牵着你的鼻子走。预见能让你成为自己命运的掌控者。你积极地设想潜在的未来，并在今天做出预防性的战略决策，这样你就永远不会完全措手不及，也不会被整个行业淘汰。一位名叫Moment的学生提出了一个极好的问题：我们是着眼于哪些通用技术将塑造未来，还是深入关注某项“特定”技术将如何演变，比如他特别感兴趣的太阳能价格下降问题？我解释说，预见在多个不同的层面上运作，这在你们阅读的Lockwood Carlson的文章中已经清楚地描绘出来了。

    如果你是一名积极将资金投入太阳能、风能或地热能的研发经理，你的预见是非常集中的。你分析你对太阳能的长期押注是否仍然合理，或者竞争对手的新兴技术是否表明你应该调整投资方向。这代表了单一业务团队或特定技术层面的预见。但预见是可以向上扩展的。它可以涵盖整个公司、整个行业、国家政府，甚至全世界。例如，从国家层面来看，新加坡政府在几年前执行了产业转型蓝图。他们仔细评估了国家预算应将研发资金押注在哪些部门，以确保未来的经济生存。事实上，国家研究基金会（NRF）目前非常有兴趣培训他们的公务员在制定政策时更具前瞻性，而这门课程正是决定国家应该把赌注押在什么上面的一项努力。当我们的客座演讲嘉宾Koo Seng Meng先生下周到来时，他将讨论他之前在NRF的工作，在那里他在庞大的国家层面上跨越多个部门应用了这些预见原则。你们在这里学到的工具可以完美地扩展，从个人职业规划一直到国家战略。

  - [19:02:50 - 19:09:16] **Analyzing the Lockwood Carlson Framework**

    I then transitioned the class to the second major question, which focused directly on Lockwood Carlson's article: "Using Technology Foresight to Create Business Value." I wanted to reward the students who had genuinely done the heavy reading prior to class. Joanne bravely went first. She synthesized that Carlson frames foresighting not merely as speculation, but as a highly structured, strategic process designed to translate emerging external technologies directly into actionable future options for a company. She astutely pointed out that the methodology revolves entirely around clearly defining the firm's current "Power Zone," creating future technology options, and forcefully integrating those findings back into the current R&D and business strategies. She also referenced the "Technology Space Map," a core tool used to broadly classify the company's internal strengths against the outer landscape. I commended Joanne, telling her she had successfully captured about fifty percent of the critical framework.

    Meredith then built upon Joanne’s foundation by focusing on the operational logistics highlighted in the paper. She emphasized that Carlson explicitly lays out a sequential, step-by-step process. More importantly, she noted that Carlson rigorously defines the absolute prerequisites for success—the most vital being unwavering sponsorship and support from top-level executive management. Meredith correctly deduced that without absolute buy-in from the C-suite, the foresighting process is utterly pointless because the resulting intelligence will never be elevated high enough to influence actual corporate strategy; it will just die at the local department level. This perfectly echoed my earlier warning that not all advanced tools are useful if the organizational culture refuses to support them.

    Lisa then added a brilliant point regarding the human element of the framework. She stated that her favorite takeaway from the article was the strict requirement to involve highly diverse, cross-functional teams. Carlson insists on bringing together junior and senior technical staff, marketing experts, business developers, and crucially, external outside experts. Lisa explained that conducting these analyses across two separated workshop sessions with such diverse minds is the only way to effectively neutralize toxic "groupthink," forcing the team into uncomfortable divergent thinking before pulling them back for convergent analysis. I enthusiastically validated her point, noting that executives simply cannot operate in isolated silos, making dictatorial decisions without cross-functional friction. Another student chimed in, pointing out that Carlson emphasizes the selection of a highly capable, neutral facilitator. I agreed entirely; a facilitator who commands professional technical respect but possesses the soft skills to manage volatile, conflicting opinions and maintain strict process discipline is the linchpin of the whole operation.

    The core philosophy to internalize here is that foresighting is fundamentally a *process*. It is not a crystal ball declaring, "This is exactly what will happen." It is a structured, collaborative methodology that prepares a firm for multiple potential realities. Unfortunately, in many real-world organizations—especially small and medium enterprises (SMEs)—upper management fails to understand this value. They are so consumed with managing their daily operational fires and securing tomorrow's bread and butter that foresighting seems like an absurd luxury. This is why agencies like A*STAR actively intervene in Singapore, literally holding the hands of these SMEs, running workshops for them, and desperately warning them that if they do not look up from their daily grind, a future technology will completely obliterate their business model. In massive corporations, you have the financial luxury to run these extensive foresighting workshops, which often involve pulling dozens of highly paid experts into a posh resort or spa for days of uninterrupted thinking. Naturally, skeptical bosses view this as a massive, tangible cost and aggressively demand immediate, tangible KPIs. If you cannot demonstrably prove the financial value of these retreats, the program gets killed. Next week, we will dive deep into exactly how you construct the arguments to convince stubborn management that investing in this foresighting process is the only thing standing between them and bankruptcy.

    然后，我将课堂引向了第二个主要问题，该问题直接集中在Lockwood Carlson的文章上：“利用技术预见创造商业价值”。我想奖励那些在课前真正完成了大量阅读的学生。Joanne勇敢地第一个发言。她总结道，Carlson并没有仅仅将预见框架视为推测，而是将其视为一个高度结构化的战略过程，旨在将新兴的外部技术直接转化为公司可执行的未来选项。她敏锐地指出，该方法论完全围绕清晰地定义公司当前的“实力区”（Power Zone）、创造未来技术选项，并将这些发现强有力地整合回当前的研发和业务战略中。她还提到了“技术空间图谱”（Technology Space Map），这是一个核心工具，用于将公司的内部优势与外部环境进行广泛的分类对比。我表扬了Joanne，告诉她她已经成功地掌握了大约百分之五十的关键框架。

    随后，Meredith在Joanne的基础之上，将重点放在了论文中强调的运营后勤上。她强调，Carlson明确地制定了一个循序渐进的流程。更重要的是，她指出，Carlson严格定义了成功的绝对先决条件——最重要的是来自最高执行管理层坚定不移的赞助和支持。Meredith正确地推断出，如果没有最高管理层的绝对支持，预见过程是毫无意义的，因为产生的情报永远不会被提升到足以影响实际公司战略的高度；它只会死在地方部门层面。这完美地呼应了我早先的警告：如果组织文化拒绝支持，并非所有先进的工具都是有用的。

    接着，Lisa补充了一个关于框架中人的因素的精彩观点。她说她从这篇文章中最喜欢的一点是，文章严格要求组建高度多样化、跨职能的团队。Carlson坚持将初级和高级技术人员、营销专家、业务开发人员，以及至关重要的外部专家聚集在一起。Lisa解释说，与如此多样化的人才分两次研讨会进行这些分析，是有效中和有害的“群体思维”（groupthink）的唯一途径，迫使团队在拉回进行收敛分析之前，进行令人不适的发散思维。我热情地肯定了她的观点，指出高管们根本无法在孤立的筒仓中运作，在没有跨职能摩擦的情况下做出独断专行的决定。另一位学生插话指出，Carlson强调选择一位能力极强、中立的引导者。我完全同意；一位能够赢得专业技术尊重，同时具备处理多变、冲突意见并维持严格流程纪律的软技能的引导者，是整个运作的关键。

    这里需要内化的核心理念是，预见从根本上说是一个“过程”。它不是一个宣称“这一定会发生”的水晶球。它是一种结构化的、协作的方法论，使公司为多重潜在的现实做好准备。不幸的是，在许多现实世界的组织中——尤其是中小型企业（SME）——高层管理人员未能理解这种价值。他们如此沉迷于处理日常运营的紧急情况并确保明天的生计，以至于预见似乎是一种荒谬的奢侈品。这就是为什么像新加坡科技研究局（A*STAR）这样的机构积极在新加坡干预，手把手地指导这些中小企业，为他们举办研讨会，并绝望地警告他们，如果他们不从日常的苦差事中抬起头来，未来的技术将彻底摧毁他们的商业模式。在大型企业中，你有财力开展这些广泛的预见研讨会，这通常涉及将几十位高薪专家拉到一个豪华的度假村或水疗中心，进行数天不受干扰的思考。自然，持怀疑态度的老板会将此视为巨大的有形成本，并强烈要求立即获得切实的KPI。如果你不能令人信服地证明这些静修的财务价值，该项目就会被取消。下周，我们将深入探讨你到底如何构建论据，以说服固执的管理层：投资于这种预见过程是防止他们破产的唯一屏障。

  - [19:09:16 - 19:12:11] **Group Discussion on Analytical Tools**

    (The class transitioned into a brief offline activity where students discussed and reviewed the specific analytical tools mentioned by Carlson, such as the Technology Space Matrix, before regrouping to discuss how to structure a foresight workshop.)

    (全班转入了一个简短的线下活动，学生们讨论并回顾了Carlson提到的特定分析工具，比如技术空间矩阵，然后重新集合讨论如何构建一个预见研讨会。)

  - [19:12:11 - 19:14:18] **Framing the Foresight Question and Actionable Outputs**

    As you construct your foresighting strategy, you can utilize complex frameworks like the Technology Space Map and Power Zones. However, trust me, when I was previously consulting with a colleague comparing the competitive futures of wind turbine technology versus solar technology, we managed to lay out the entire foresighting analysis using a simple, beautifully structured Excel spreadsheet. The complexity of the tool matters far less than the precision of your core objective. At the conclusion of that crucial first workshop, the management absolutely must carve out a highly focused, neatly framed core question that dictates exactly where the company wants to go. If you attempt to be broadly futuristic and set an open-ended goal like, "I want to remain competitive five years from now," your research parameters become endless, chaotic, and completely useless. The framing question must anchor the entire intelligence team.

    For example, going back to the earlier student's interest, a precise framing question for a corporate leader would be: "We have heavily bet our R&D capital on solar technology. Based on emerging alternatives, does it make strategic sense to double down and invest more in solar, or should we pivot?" For my own career, as a tenured professor teaching and researching at NUS, my framing question is: "Is it safe to continue on my current academic trajectory, or is Artificial Intelligence going to disrupt the higher education industry so radically that I need to completely tear down and revamp my technical skill set?" That is a tightly framed anchor.

    Once the bosses define this overarching framework at the end of the first workshop, the intelligence team is dispatched to aggressively gather external data regarding industry trends and technology dynamics. You are not just randomly guessing the future; you are synthesizing this newly gathered data to inform the three critical strategic outputs highlighted in Carlson's article. These are the actionable growth opportunities decision-makers actually care about: First, "Enhance the Power Zone," which means identifying must-have technologies to fortify your current core competencies. Second, "Extend the Power Zone," which involves stretching your existing strengths into entirely adjacent, lucrative new markets. Third, identifying "New Technology Opportunities," which are radical, distant technologies that could unlock entirely new, unprecedented business avenues. All the data gathering and analysis we do is ultimately in service of answering those three strategic directives.

    当你构建你的预见战略时，你可以利用技术空间图谱和实力区等复杂的框架。但是，相信我，当我之前与一位同事为比较风力涡轮机技术和太阳能技术的竞争未来提供咨询时，我们仅使用一个简单、结构完美的Excel电子表格就成功地列出了整个预见分析。工具的复杂性远不如核心目标的精确性重要。在那次至关重要的第一次研讨会结束时，管理层绝对必须制定出一个高度集中、框架清晰的核心问题，以准确指示公司的发展方向。如果你试图广泛地展望未来，并设定一个开放式的目标，比如“我想在五年后保持竞争力”，你的研究范围就会变得无穷无尽、混乱不堪，而且毫无用处。这个框架问题必须成为整个情报团队的锚点。

    例如，回到早先那位学生感兴趣的话题，对于企业领导者来说，一个精确的框架问题应该是：“我们已经在太阳能技术上投入了大量研发资金。基于新兴的替代方案，加倍投入并在太阳能领域投资更多在战略上是否合理，还是我们应该转移投资方向？”对于我自己的职业生涯，作为一名在新加坡国立大学从事教学和研究的终身教授，我的框架问题是：“继续我目前的学术轨迹是否安全，还是人工智能会彻底颠覆高等教育行业，以至于我需要完全打破并重塑我的技术技能组合？”这就是一个框架严密的锚点。

    一旦老板们在第一次研讨会结束时定义了这个总体框架，情报团队就会被派去积极收集有关行业趋势和技术动态的外部数据。你不是在随意猜测未来；你正在综合这些新收集的数据，为Carlson文章中强调的三个关键战略输出提供信息。这些正是决策者真正关心的、可执行的增长机会：首先，“增强实力区（Enhance the Power Zone）”，这意味着找出必须具备的技术，以巩固你当前的核心竞争力。其次，“扩展实力区（Extend the Power Zone）”，这涉及将你现有的优势延伸到完全相邻、利润丰厚的新市场。第三，发现“新技术机会（New Technology Opportunities）”，这些是激进的、遥远的技术，可能开启全新的、前所未有的业务途径。我们所做的所有数据收集和分析，最终都是为了服务于这三个战略指令。

  - [19:14:40 - 19:17:48] **Interactive Group Activity Setup**

    Maybe let's do a group activity now. I was actually planning for one. This is typically how I start the whole class, but I decided not to use the slides today just to grab your attention. Knowing me from MT5007, you know I usually rely heavily on slides, but today I thought I would just go through the entire first part of the lecture without them. Okay, so let's take a quick break and then dive into this class activity. Hopefully, you all can form groups by then. For this module, let's aim for groups of around five to six members.

    For this activity, I want you to act as intelligence officers and analysts. Your specific task is to help Professor Tan. He has a question: "What kind of classrooms should NUS have in 2032?"

    Now, bear in mind everything I just said: foresighting is a *process*; it is *not* a prediction. In the past, before I gave all this background information, I used to ask students to do this exact activity right at the start. Trust me, many groups would just come up with answers like, "In 2032, there will be more AI, there will be hologram professors, there will be AI chatbots acting as teaching assistants," blah, blah, blah. Trust me, that is not foresighting. If you were to take that speculative list to Professor Tan, he is going to throw it right back at you. You need to understand that foresighting is a process of painting multiple future scenarios, and to do that, you absolutely must collect data. What kind of data will you collect? What exact process will you undertake? That must be the focus of your group activity. Is this clear? Do not just tell me what the final outcome of the 2032 classroom will be. I do not want that. I want you to walk me through *how* Professor Tan—if he were to answer this question himself—should engage in intelligence activities. That is what I want you to focus on. Everyone, let's take a short break. Let's come back by 7:35 PM, do this quick activity, and then we will move on to the rest of the articles and slides.

    也许我们现在来做一个小组活动。我其实一直计划要做一个。这通常是我开始整堂课的方式，但我今天决定不使用幻灯片，只是为了吸引你们的注意力。你们在MT5007中了解我，知道我通常非常依赖幻灯片，但今天我想在没有幻灯片的情况下完成讲座的前半部分。好的，让我们快速休息一下，然后投入到这个课堂活动中。希望到那时你们都能组好队。对于这门课，我们的目标是每组大约五到六名成员。

    对于这个活动，我希望你们扮演情报官员和分析师的角色。你们的具体任务是帮助陈教授（Professor Tan）。他有一个问题：“2032年新加坡国立大学应该拥有什么样的教室？”

    现在，记住我刚才说的一切：预见是一个*过程*；它*不是*预测。过去，在提供所有这些背景信息之前，我通常会一开始就让学生做这个活动。相信我，很多小组只会想出这样的答案：“在2032年，将会有更多的人工智能，会有全息图教授，会有充当助教的AI聊天机器人”等等。相信我，那不是预见。如果你把那份推测性的清单拿给陈教授，他会直接把它扔回给你。你需要明白，预见是描绘多种未来情景的过程，要做到这一点，你绝对必须收集数据。你将收集什么样的数据？你将采取什么确切的过程？这必须是你小组活动的重点。清楚了吗？不要只告诉我2032年教室的最终结果会是什么。我不想要那个。我希望你们带我了解，如果陈教授要亲自回答这个问题，他应该*如何*参与情报活动。这就是我希望你们关注的重点。大家稍微休息一下。让我们在晚上7:35回来，快速完成这个活动，然后我们将继续讨论其余的文章和幻灯片。

  - [19:17:48 - 19:20:16] **The Role of the Intelligence Consultant**

    Just to reiterate as you get back to your seats, you are going to walk through the *process* that will help Professor Tan arrive at his decision. Whatever investments or decisions he is going to make regarding the 2032 classroom, what is the specific process you are going to adopt to aid his decision-making? Please do not make the critical mistake of deciding *for* him. That is simply not what an intelligence officer does. Do you get what I mean? This is exactly where the role of consultants becomes a little tricky in the real world. Many companies pay exorbitant fees to consultants thinking, "They will just tell me exactly what to do." Unfortunately, to make a massive strategic decision for a company, you need a tremendous amount of deep contextual knowledge and a view of the bigger picture, which only the ultimate decision-maker—in this case, Professor Tan—will have. Your job is to tell him, "These are the possible future scenarios, and I know this because I collected this specific data. Here is my substantiation. Now, based on this landscape, what do you want to decide?" You place the intelligence on a platform for him so that *he* makes the final call and places his investments. You do not decide for him. That is a rookie mistake many people make. So, tell me: what kinds of workshops will you conduct? Who exactly will be there? What specific kind of data will you collect? Let's quickly go through each group to understand your proposed process. Who wants to go first? Karishma, please go ahead, and let's have silence while we listen to her.

    大家回到座位上时，我再重申一遍，你们要演练的是帮助陈教授做出决定的*过程*。无论他将就2032年的教室做出什么投资或决定，你们将采取什么具体的过程来辅助他做出决策？请不要犯替他做决定的致命错误。这根本不是情报官员该做的事。你们明白我的意思吗？这正是现实世界中顾问的角色变得有些棘手的地方。许多公司支付高昂的费用给顾问，心里想着：“他们会直接告诉我具体该怎么做。”不幸的是，要为一家公司做出重大的战略决策，你需要大量深厚的背景知识和对大局的把控，而这只有最终决策者——在这个案例中是陈教授——才具备。你的工作是告诉他：“这些是可能的未来情景，我知道这些是因为我收集了这些具体的数据。这是我的证据。现在，基于这种大环境，你想怎么决定？”你把情报放在一个平台上呈现给他，以便*他*做出最终决定并进行投资。你不要替他做决定。这是很多人都会犯的低级错误。所以，告诉我：你们将举办什么样的研讨会？到底会有谁参加？你们将收集什么具体种类的数据？让我们快速过一遍每个小组，了解你们提议的过程。谁想先来？Karishma，请讲，大家安静听她讲。

  - [19:20:16 - 19:25:25] **Critique of Group 1: Narrowing the Framing Question**

    Karishma presented her group's approach, stating that they focused heavily on helping students pick up skills faster for the job market. They based this on surveys showing that undergraduates and postgraduates are primarily concerned about securing jobs now. I paused her there and addressed the class. Her group's assumption is that the primary goal of the 2032 classroom is to help students be better placed in the job market. I asked the class: "How many of you like this approach of having a clearly, narrowly defined framing question?" I then asked, "How many of you do not like it, and why?" One student pointed out that they weren't entirely sure that specific problem—current job anxieties—would still be the dominant problem in 2032. Another student correctly argued that it was narrowing the scope too much, ignoring that a university classroom is filled with people who have multiple different goals beyond just finding a corporate job. I clarified that Karishma's group didn't necessarily do anything wrong—I wasn't trying to nail them down. Having a narrow question is fine *if* you actually consulted with the decision-maker first. If you had gone to Professor Tan and asked, "What is your main intention?" and he replied, "My students complain they aren't getting placed, I want to fix that for the future," then their narrow problem statement would be perfectly valid. However, if they just assumed that was the goal without asking, that is problematic. As analysts, you must interface with your decision-maker first to understand what they truly want. If you just take a broad prompt, assume a narrow goal, and run with it, you are doing it wrong.

    Karishma then elaborated that they realized the scope was too narrow, so they looked at the "NUS 120" vision documents to see what the university was already planning for the next 5 to 10 years. They saw alignments with national goals like sustainability, health, innovation, and the Smart Nation initiative. They dug deeper into NUS's specific focus on research centers and entrepreneurship hubs. This led them to reframe their question from just "picking up job skills" to preparing students for a rapidly evolving, diverse landscape. I praised this pivot, noting that this is exactly how the intelligence process should organically evolve. Karishma concluded that based on these aligned visions, they mapped out different scenarios—one focused purely on jobs, another heavily on entrepreneurship backed by NUS's new venture funding—and decided they would gather data specifically aligned with those diverging scenarios.

    Karishma展示了她所在小组的方法，说他们主要关注帮助学生更快地掌握就业市场所需的技能。他们的依据是调查显示，本科生和研究生目前最关心的是找工作。我打断了她并向全班提问。她所在小组的假设是，2032年教室的首要目标是帮助学生在就业市场上处于更有利的位置。我问全班：“你们中有多少人喜欢这种设定一个清晰、狭窄的框架问题的方法？”然后我又问：“你们中有多少人不喜欢，为什么？”一位学生指出，他们不能完全确定那个特定的问题——当前的就业焦虑——在2032年是否仍然会是主要问题。另一位学生准确地指出，这把范围缩小得太多了，忽略了大学教室里充满了有着除了找公司工作之外多种不同目标的人。我澄清说，Karishma的小组未必做错了什么——我不是想为难他们。*如果*你实际上先咨询了决策者，那么有一个狭窄的问题是没问题的。如果你去问陈教授：“你的主要意图是什么？”他回答说：“我的学生抱怨他们找不到工作，我想在未来解决这个问题，”那么他们狭窄的问题陈述就完全有效了。然而，如果他们不问就假设那是目标，那就有问题了。作为分析师，你必须首先与你的决策者沟通，以了解他们真正想要什么。如果你只是接受一个宽泛的提示，假设一个狭窄的目标，然后就照着做，那你就做错了。

    Karishma接着详细说明，他们意识到范围太窄了，所以他们查看了“NUS 120”愿景文件，看看大学已经为未来5到10年规划了什么。他们看到了与可持续发展、健康、创新和智慧国（Smart Nation）倡议等国家目标的契合。他们深入研究了新加坡国立大学对研究中心和创业中心的具体关注。这促使他们重新构建了他们的问题，从仅仅“掌握工作技能”转变为让学生为快速发展、多样化的环境做好准备。我赞扬了这种转变，指出这正是情报过程应该如何有机发展的。Karishma总结说，基于这些一致的愿景，他们描绘了不同的情景——一个纯粹关注就业，另一个在新加坡国立大学新的风险投资支持下重点关注创业——并决定他们将专门收集与这些不同情景相一致的数据。

  - [19:25:25 - 19:30:10] **Expanding the Scope of Data Collection**

    I then pushed Karishma's group further on exactly *how* and from *whom* they would collect this data. She suggested using surveys to ask the current student population and faculty. I challenged this immediately: "Are current students really the right focus group?" Another student interjected, correctly pointing out that current students are anchored in the present, not the future. I agreed, explaining that while a focus group is the right methodology, you need to involve futuristic thinkers. You should be talking to future students currently in secondary schools, or consulting with Ministry of Education (MOE) policymakers. You must even look into the evolving learning psychology of the next generation, because how you learn today is completely different from how my young son learns now. If Professor Tan just blasts out a mandatory survey to current NUS students, he is just collecting hindsight. As an intelligence analyst, your job is to find the data he cannot easily access himself.

    I shared a real example: a couple of years ago, when Professor Tan was pondering similar futuristic questions, he was closely monitoring a Chinese company called Ping An. He was deeply impressed by how rapidly they were evolving across the finance and medical sectors, and he wanted NUS to match that agility. That is the level at which decision-makers operate—they are looking at cross-industry transformations. Therefore, you cannot confine your intelligence gathering solely to the education sector. I asked the class: "Can you think of entities completely outside of the traditional education sector that are currently threatening to dramatically disrupt it?" A student correctly identified tech companies. Exactly. Massive tech giants are starting their own rigorous training programs and issuing their own recognized certifications. Today's youth are already asking, "Why should I spend years at a university and struggle to find a job when I can just get trained directly by Google or Microsoft and get absorbed into their workforce immediately?" If tech giants aggressively enter the education space, what will NUS or NTU do? Professor Tan desperately needs to think about that, especially regarding our Master's programs. Intelligence gathering is not just about researching classroom infrastructure or hiring better teachers; it is about analyzing broader industry threats. Should Professor Tan proactively collaborate with these tech giants? That is vital intelligence. As an intelligence expert, your absolute first duty is to expose your decision-maker to all potential external threats and radical opportunities so they are prepared.

    然后我进一步追问Karishma的小组，他们究竟将*如何*以及从*谁*那里收集这些数据。她建议使用调查问卷来询问在校学生和教职员工。我立刻对这一点提出了质疑：“现在的学生真的是合适的焦点小组吗？”另一名学生插话，准确地指出现在的学生立足于现在，而不是未来。我表示同意，并解释说，虽然焦点小组是正确的方法，但你需要让具有未来思维的人参与进来。你应该与目前在中学就读的未来学生交谈，或者咨询教育部（MOE）的政策制定者。你甚至必须研究下一代不断演变的学习心理学，因为你们现在的学习方式与我年幼的儿子现在的学习方式完全不同。如果陈教授只是向当前的新加坡国立大学学生强制发送一份调查问卷，他收集到的只是事后诸葛亮的数据。作为一名情报分析师，你的工作是找到他自己无法轻易获取的数据。

    我分享了一个真实的例子：几年前，当陈教授在思考类似的未来问题时，他正在密切关注一家名为中国平安的中国公司。他对他们跨越金融和医疗领域的快速发展印象深刻，他希望新加坡国立大学也能具备同样的敏捷性。这就是决策者运作的层面——他们着眼于跨行业的转型。因此，你不能将情报收集仅仅局限于教育部门。我问全班同学：“你们能想到完全在传统教育部门之外，目前正威胁要大幅颠覆它的实体吗？”一名学生准确地指出了科技公司。完全正确。大型科技巨头正在开展自己严格的培训计划，并颁发自己受认可的证书。今天的年轻人已经在问：“如果我能直接接受谷歌或微软的培训，并立即加入他们的员工队伍，为什么我还要在大学里耗费数年，然后还要努力找工作呢？”如果科技巨头大举进入教育领域，新加坡国立大学或南洋理工大学会怎么做？陈教授迫切需要考虑这一点，尤其是关于我们的硕士项目。情报收集不仅仅是研究教室的基础设施或聘请更好的老师；它是关于分析更广泛的行业威胁。陈教授应该主动与这些科技巨头合作吗？这是至关重要的情报。作为一名情报专家，你的首要职责是向你的决策者揭示所有潜在的外部威胁和激进的机会，让他们做好准备。

  - [19:30:10 - 19:36:50] **Critique of Group 2: Confusing Hindsight with Foresight**

    Next, Zuhair and Jared's group presented. Zuhair explained that they tried to apply the "Hindsight, Insight, Foresight" strategy. For hindsight, they tracked the evolution of information sharing—from chalkboards, to presentations, to the rapid digitalization during COVID-19, leading to the current hybrid model where documents are shared before class even begins. Their insight was that since information is now easily accessible, the current challenge is fostering actual classroom engagement rather than mere information transfer. Jared then extrapolated this into the future, suggesting specific technological solutions like interactive desk buttons, learning from how parliaments or government sectors operate. He also heavily emphasized implementing VR headsets, suggesting students could visualize complex environments or run dangerous chemistry experiments virtually without risk, keeping them highly engaged. Finally, he briefly mentioned a more radical idea: using brainwave monitoring to allow students to interact with whiteboards mentally.

    I gave them my quick critique: While the thought process was good, their initial recommendations were almost entirely based on hindsight and present-day reality, not true foresight. For instance, I pointed out that the VR chemistry lab idea they presented as a futuristic solution *already exists* right here at NUS. The Chemical Engineering department currently uses VR because they cannot safely take students to real chemical plants. It is already implemented. This highlights a critical lesson from Carlson’s framework regarding the "Power Zone": many times, in a massive organization, information is so siloed that you don't even know what your own company is already doing. You might pitch a "futuristic" idea that a different department deployed two years ago! That is why thoroughly understanding your present Power Zone is the mandatory first step. I clarified that I wasn't shooting them down, but emphasizing that they must push past existing tech.

    I did, however, praise Jared's mention of brainwave monitoring, noting that this is genuinely futuristic. I reminded the class of a video I showed in MT5007 about what is currently happening in China, where students wear headbands that use AI to monitor their brainwaves to see if they are focusing, sending real-time data to the teacher. This opens up entirely new intelligence avenues: while the technology exists, the global ethical backlash is massive. People argue it is exploitative and unethical. As an intelligence officer, if you present this brainwave technology to Professor Tan as a potential future classroom tool, you absolutely must also provide the intelligence regarding the severe ethical pitfalls and regulatory risks associated with it.

    接下来是Zuhair和Jared的小组展示。Zuhair解释说，他们试图应用“后见、洞察、预见”的策略。在回顾过去时，他们追踪了信息共享的演变——从黑板到演示文稿，再到新冠疫情期间的快速数字化，最终演变成目前的混合模式，即在上课前就共享文件。他们的洞察是，既然现在信息很容易获取，当前的挑战是促进实际的课堂参与，而不仅仅是信息传递。Jared随后将其推断到未来，提出了一些具体的技术解决方案，例如交互式桌面按钮，借鉴议会或政府部门的运作方式。他还非常强调应用VR头显，建议学生可以直观地看到复杂的环境，或者在没有风险的情况下虚拟地进行危险的化学实验，让他们保持高度的参与度。最后，他简要地提到了一个更激进的想法：使用脑电波监测让学生在精神上与白板互动。

    我给出了我的快速点评：虽然思维过程很好，但他们最初的建议几乎完全基于后见之明和现状，而不是真正的预见。例如，我指出他们作为未来解决方案提出的VR化学实验室在新加坡国立大学“已经存在”了。化学工程系目前正在使用VR，因为他们无法安全地带学生去真正的化工厂。它已经投入使用了。这突出了Carlson框架中关于“实力区”的一个关键教训：很多时候，在一个庞大的组织中，信息是如此孤立，以至于你甚至不知道你自己的公司已经在做什么。你可能会推销一个其他部门两年前就已经部署的“未来”想法！这就是为什么彻底了解你目前的实力区是强制性的第一步。我澄清说我不是在打击他们，而是在强调他们必须超越现有的技术。

    不过，我赞扬了Jared提到的脑电波监测，指出这确实具有未来感。我提醒全班同学，我在MT5007课上放过一个关于中国目前正在发生的事情的视频，在那儿学生们戴着使用AI监测脑电波的发带，看看他们是否在专心，并将实时数据发送给老师。这开辟了全新的情报途径：虽然技术存在，但全球范围内的伦理反弹是巨大的。人们认为这是剥削和不道德的。作为一名情报官员，如果你向陈教授展示这种脑电波技术作为潜在的未来课堂工具，你绝对必须同时提供关于其严重的伦理陷阱和相关监管风险的情报。

  - [19:36:50 - 19:41:35] **Synthesizing the Ideal Foresight Process**

    Finally, a last group shared a very streamlined approach: they stated they would quickly secure experienced teachers, immediately research future trends, and then map out different scenarios to enhance current strengths against other countries. I praised this because it perfectly captured the *process* flow I was looking for. I summarized the ideal sequence for the class: First, as the intelligence officer, you sit down with Professor Tan to aggressively narrow down the true scope and intent of his question. Second, you assemble a highly diverse focus group workshop. Crucially, as Carlson’s article demands, this group must include people from entirely different business areas—not just teachers and students, but IT infrastructure experts, campus security, and people from other faculties. Why? Because if you propose a VR idea, the chemical engineering guy will immediately tell you they already did it. If you propose AI brainwaves, the computer science expert will immediately brief you on the ethical disaster happening in China. Bringing these diverse stakeholders together immediately pools fractured information and prevents redundant work.

    After that initial workshop, you assign these diverse stakeholders specific, targeted areas to research. They go out, gather fresh external data, and return for the second workshop. Here, they present their trend analysis. Based on this rich data, you paint three or four drastically different potential scenarios for the 2032 classroom. You lay these scenarios in front of Professor Tan. He does not decide, "This is the single future we are building." Instead, he decides how to spread his investments to be safe. Even knowing the ethical risks, he might invest heavily in brainwave tech if he believes distraction is an existential threat to learning. Or, he might bet heavily on holographic tech to pull in global industry experts seamlessly. He places strategic bets on the directions that seem most worthwhile. Your job is to facilitate the data collection, engage the right minds, and ensure the decision-maker is completely synergistic with the intelligence process. Another student noted this sounds very similar to general problem-solving. I agreed it shares DNA with problem-solving—which can range from tactical to operational—but foresighting is uniquely strategic and entirely focused on navigating deep future uncertainty.

    最后，最后一个小组分享了一个非常精简的方法：他们表示，他们将迅速锁定有经验的教师，立即研究未来趋势，然后描绘不同的情景，以增强相对于其他国家的现有优势。我赞扬了这一点，因为它完美地抓住了我正在寻找的“过程”流程。我为全班总结了理想的顺序：首先，作为情报官员，你坐下来与陈教授深入探讨，以极大地缩小他问题的真实范围和意图。其次，你召集一个高度多样化的焦点小组研讨会。至关重要的是，正如Carlson的文章所要求的那样，这个小组必须包括来自完全不同业务领域的人——不仅仅是老师和学生，还包括IT基础设施专家、校园安保人员以及来自其他院系的人员。为什么？因为如果你提出一个VR的想法，化学工程的人会立刻告诉你他们已经这么做了。如果你提出AI脑电波，计算机科学专家会立刻向你简要介绍中国正在发生的伦理灾难。将这些不同的利益相关者聚集在一起，可以立即汇集零碎的信息，并防止重复工作。

    在那次初步研讨会之后，你分配给这些不同的利益相关者具体的、有针对性的领域进行研究。他们出去收集新鲜的外部数据，然后回来参加第二次研讨会。在这里，他们展示他们的趋势分析。基于这些丰富的数据，你为2032年的教室描绘了三到四个截然不同的潜在情景。你把这些情景摆在陈教授面前。他并不是决定：“这就是我们将要构建的唯一未来。”相反，他决定如何分散投资以确保安全。即使知道伦理风险，如果他认为分心是对学习的生存威胁，他也可能会在脑电波技术上投入巨资。或者，他可能会在全息技术上下重注，以无缝地引进全球行业专家。他在看起来最有价值的方向上进行战略押注。你的工作是促进数据收集，让合适的人才参与进来，并确保决策者与情报过程完全协同。另一名学生指出这听起来非常类似于一般的问题解决。我同意它与解决问题（可以从战术层面到运营层面）有共同点，但预见具有独特的战略性，并且完全专注于驾驭深远的未来不确定性。

  - [19:41:35 - 19:50:31] **Mentimeter Quiz and the Agile Nature of Roadmaps**

    Returning to the lecture notes, I pulled up a quick Mentimeter quiz to test their understanding of the Lockwood Carlson article and to demonstrate the interactive format of future classes. The first question asked if technology foresight identifies threats, opportunities, or both. The class easily agreed it was both, which I had verbally covered earlier. The next question asked if technology foresight ignores the present to look only at the future. I emphatically reminded them that you absolutely cannot ignore the present. True foresighting demands that you know exactly where your "Power Zone" currently is so you can map the path from today to those potential futures five or ten years away.

    The third question was critical: Is technology foresight a one-time activity, an ongoing process, or both? I was very happy to see that no one answered "one-time activity." However, I had to deliberately pause and explain the harsh reality. In an ideal world, it is an ongoing process. But practically, many real-world organizations treat it as a one-off event. They lack the resources, culture, or visionary leadership to sustain it, so they run one workshop, build a rigid roadmap, and treat it like a Bible. I asked the class if they knew what a "roadmap" was, explaining it is basically charting where you are, where you want to go, and the steps to get there. If a company treats a roadmap as a rigid, one-time document, they are guaranteed to fail. A roadmap must be incredibly agile. I used a sailing analogy: If you are the captain of a ship with many passengers, you know your final destination. But can you stubbornly plot one single, unchangeable route? Absolutely not. You have to constantly adjust for changing winds, dangerous tides, and unpredictable currents. Foresighting is not about blindly following a Bible; it is about knowing how to dynamically navigate your investments as new scenarios arise, ensuring you aren't trapped in a dead-end technology. The article technically answers "both," because while it *should* be ongoing, many poorly resourced SMEs can only afford to do it once.

    We then briefly touched on the scope of foresighting, agreeing it happens at every level—from individual career planning to massive global initiatives like multi-nation pacts tackling CO2 emissions. Finally, I asked if foresighting must strictly be triggered top-down by management. A student practically noted that top-down is required to actually secure funding and buy-in. Another student countered that ideally, it should be bottom-up, triggered by anyone who spots a critical trend. I explained that while many hierarchical companies force a top-down approach, the most innovative organizations cultivate a bottom-up culture where ground-level intelligence flows upward. We will explore the friction between hierarchical and intelligent organizations in Week 4.

    回到讲义，我调出了一个简短的Mentimeter测验，以测试他们对Lockwood Carlson文章的理解，并展示未来课程的互动形式。第一个问题问技术预见是识别威胁、机会，还是两者兼有。全班很容易地达成共识，认为是两者兼有，我早先已经口头讲过了。下一个问题问技术预见是否忽略现在只看未来。我着重提醒他们，你绝对不能忽略现在。真正的预见要求你确切地知道你目前的“实力区”在哪里，这样你才能描绘出从今天到五年或十年后那些潜在未来的路径。

    第三个问题很关键：技术预见是一次性活动、持续的过程，还是两者兼有？我很高兴看到没有人回答“一次性活动”。然而，我不得不刻意停顿下来，解释残酷的现实。在一个理想的世界里，它是一个持续的过程。但在现实中，许多现实世界的组织把它当作一次性的事件来对待。他们缺乏资源、文化或有远见的领导力来维持它，所以他们举办一次研讨会，制定一个僵化的路线图，然后把它当成圣经。我问全班同学是否知道什么是“路线图（roadmap）”，并解释说这基本上就是规划你现在在哪里、你想去哪里以及到达那里的步骤。如果一家公司把路线图当作一份僵化的、一次性的文件，他们注定会失败。路线图必须极其敏捷。我用航海做了一个比喻：如果你是一艘载有许多乘客的船的船长，你知道你的最终目的地。但你能固执地规划出一条单一的、不可改变的路线吗？绝对不能。你必须根据不断变化的风向、危险的潮汐和不可预测的洋流不断进行调整。预见不是盲目地遵循圣经；它是关于知道随着新情况的出现，如何动态地引导你的投资，确保你不会陷入技术的死胡同。这篇文章在技术上回答了“两者兼有”，因为虽然它“应该”是持续的，但许多资源匮乏的中小企业只能负担得起做一次。

    然后我们简要地触及了预见的范围，同意它发生在每一个层面——从个人职业规划到像应对二氧化碳排放的多国协议这样庞大的全球倡议。最后，我问预见是否必须严格由管理层自上而下地触发。一名学生从实际出发指出，自上而下是实际获得资金和支持所必需的。另一名学生反驳说，理想情况下，它应该是自下而上的，由任何发现关键趋势的人触发。我解释说，虽然许多等级森严的公司强制采用自上而下的方法，但最具创新性的组织会培养一种自下而上的文化，让基层的智慧向上流动。我们将在第四周探讨等级森严的组织与智能型组织之间的摩擦。

  - [19:50:31 - 19:56:49] **The Three Strategic Decisions of Foresighting**

    I wrapped up the discussion on Carlson's framework by explicitly detailing the three final strategic decisions an organization must make after completing the foresighting process. First, you must decide what aspects of your Power Zone to **Enhance**. Using myself as an example, my Power Zone is teaching, research, and service. If my gathered intelligence indicates that AI is fully automating traditional lectures, then traditional teaching might be a dead end. Therefore, I must intentionally choose to enhance my research skills, specifically integrating AI into my portfolio, to survive. However, if the data shows that students still deeply crave human empathy that AI cannot provide, then I must double down and enhance my interpersonal teaching skills.

    Second, you decide what to **Extend**. If my current research does not involve Machine Learning, but the industry is undeniably moving that way, I must extend my existing research capabilities to include ML techniques, stretching my Power Zone into adjacent territory.

    Third, you must identify **New Opportunities** to exploit. If tech companies are bypassing universities and creating their own private educational ecosystems, I have to ask myself: Should I remain exclusively loyal to NUS, or should I take a massive risk and start heavily collaborating with corporate training centers? Embracing new opportunities often requires risking your current stability, much like a metallurgy company abandoning core products to invest in untested alloys, or abandoning solar to pivot to geothermal. The entire purpose of the power zone mapping, the workshops, and the data gathering is to formulate a strategy that answers these three exact questions, thereby mitigating fatal threats and exploiting lucrative new frontiers. I skipped over the complex, centroid-based mathematical slides detailing how to plot these zones, reminding the students not to get lost in the micro-techniques, as different companies use drastically different plotting methods. The overarching process is what truly matters.

    我通过明确详细地说明一个组织在完成预见过程后必须做出的三个最终战略决策，结束了对Carlson框架的讨论。首先，你必须决定**增强（Enhance）**你实力区的哪些方面。以我自己为例，我的实力区是教学、研究和服务。如果我收集到的情报表明，人工智能正在将传统讲座完全自动化，那么传统教学可能是一条死胡同。因此，我必须刻意选择提高我的研究技能，特别是将AI整合到我的投资组合中，以求生存。然而，如果数据显示学生仍然深深渴望AI无法提供的人类同理心，那么我必须加倍努力并提高我的人际教学技能。

    其次，你决定**扩展（Extend）**什么。如果我目前的研究不涉及机器学习，但毫无疑问行业正在朝着这个方向发展，我必须扩展我现有的研究能力以包括ML技术，将我的实力区延伸到相邻的领域。

    第三，你必须找出可以利用的**新机会（New Opportunities）**。如果科技公司绕过大学，建立自己的私人教育生态系统，我不得不问自己：我应该继续完全忠诚于新加坡国立大学，还是应该冒着巨大的风险开始与企业培训中心大力合作？拥抱新机会通常需要拿你目前的稳定性冒险，就像一家冶金公司放弃核心产品去投资未经测试的合金，或者放弃太阳能转向地热能一样。绘制实力区图、举办研讨会和收集数据的全部目的，就是制定一个准确回答这三个问题的战略，从而减轻致命威胁并利用利润丰厚的新领域。我跳过了详细说明如何绘制这些区域的、复杂的、基于质心的数学幻灯片，提醒学生们不要迷失在微观技术中，因为不同的公司使用的绘制方法截然不同。真正重要的是总体的过程。

  - [19:56:49 - 20:02:20] **Terminology: Scouting, Monitoring, and the Evolution to Foresight**

    I moved on to clarify some specific industry terminology. While "intelligence" might be a broad term, you must understand activities like Technology Scouting and Technology Monitoring. I asked the class to define technology scouting. Big companies do this constantly: they aggressively survey the landscape to find startup companies or university research labs developing top-notch, disruptive technologies, and they simply buy them out or absorb their research. Technology monitoring, on the other hand, is highly targeted. For instance, anyone in the educational technology sector who is serious about AI will obsessively monitor Georgia Tech. Why? Because the professors there are famous for developing cutting-edge AI teaching tools and secretly deploying them in their own classrooms long before they ever hit the commercial market. As an intelligence specialist, knowing to monitor Georgia Tech gives your decision-maker a massive competitive advantage.

    I then explained the historical evolution from simple forecasting to complex foresighting. In the past, when supply chains were simple and localized, forecasting one or two steps ahead based on historical data was sufficient. But today, the environment is violently dynamic. I shared an anecdote about a colleague, Bert, who ran a massive foresighting project for the company that makes Oreo cookies. When the Ukraine-Russia war broke out, a critical, obscure ingredient for Oreos that was sourced exclusively from that region suddenly vanished. A massive global brand was instantly paralyzed by a geopolitical conflict half a world away. They desperately had to foresee plant-based alternatives to keep production alive. This proved that intelligence cannot be narrow-minded. You cannot just look at your immediate technology; you must analyze the macro socio-economic and geopolitical environment over a long horizon. That realization is why modern organizations abandoned rigid forecasting and embraced fluid foresighting.

    我接着澄清了一些具体的行业术语。虽然“情报”可能是一个宽泛的术语，但你必须了解技术搜寻（Technology Scouting）和技术监控（Technology Monitoring）等活动。我让全班同学定义技术搜寻。大公司经常这么做：他们积极地调查市场，寻找开发顶尖、颠覆性技术的初创公司或大学研究实验室，然后干脆将它们买断或吸收它们的研究成果。另一方面，技术监控则非常有针对性。例如，任何在教育技术领域认真对待AI的人都会痴迷地监控佐治亚理工学院（Georgia Tech）。为什么？因为那里的教授以开发尖端的人工智能教学工具而闻名，并且在它们进入商业市场之前很久，就秘密地将它们部署在自己的课堂上。作为一名情报专家，知道去监控佐治亚理工学院能给你的决策者带来巨大的竞争优势。

    然后我解释了从简单的预测到复杂的预见的历史演变。在过去，当供应链简单且本地化时，根据历史数据预测未来一两步就足够了。但今天，环境剧烈动荡。我分享了关于同事Bert的一件轶事，他为生产奥利奥（Oreo）饼干的公司进行了一个庞大的预见项目。当乌克兰-俄罗斯战争爆发时，一种专门从该地区采购的奥利奥关键、冷门原料突然断货。一个庞大的全球品牌瞬间被半个地球之外的地缘政治冲突所瘫痪。他们不得不拼命寻找基于植物的替代品来维持生产。这证明了情报不能目光短浅。你不能只盯着眼前的技术；你必须在一个较长的时间跨度内分析宏观的社会经济和地缘政治环境。这种认识正是现代组织放弃僵化的预测转而拥抱流动的预见的原因。

  - [20:02:20 - 20:07:27] **Module Roadmap and Group Project Details**

    Quickly covering the module structure: The first half is heavily theoretical—understanding what intelligence is and how it is structured. The second half is intensely hands-on, focusing on specific tools like the Delphi method, bibliometric analysis, scenario analysis, and roadmapping. I noted that I used to teach Patent Data Analytics within this module, but analyzing patents to find "white spaces" for R&D is such an incredibly vast ocean of knowledge that I actually spun it off into its own entirely separate module offered this semester. If you are serious about foresighting, those two modules go hand-in-hand. Because the second half is highly analytical and utilizes open-source software and Excel, I will provide the core instructional steps via pre-recorded videos. This allows the data experts in the class to skim rapidly, while beginners can pause and work step-by-step at their own pace. We have several guest lectures planned, including Seng Meng next week and Renee from France in Week 5. After the long Chinese New Year break, I will cover Knowledge Management. I initially planned to travel, but decided to stay and push through the material because the large class size means we desperately need two full weeks just for final presentations.

    Regarding those final group projects: You have two choices. The superior option is an open-ended project where you analyze the actual intelligence activities of a real company—for example, mapping out how SP Group dictates national energy intelligence, or how a specific startup navigates its space. If you lack industry access or work experience, you can use the fallback option provided in Canvas: a case study on "Straumann," a Swiss SME. Let me be brutally frank: groups that hustle to do an open-ended project on a real company will absolutely score higher than those who just present the pre-packaged Straumann case. Straumann is merely a hygiene factor for those with zero experience; do the open-ended project if you want top marks.

    快速介绍课程结构：前半部分侧重理论——了解什么是情报以及它是如何构建的。后半部分则是高强度的实践，重点介绍具体工具，如德尔菲法（Delphi method）、文献计量分析（bibliometric analysis）、情景分析（scenario analysis）和路线图制定（roadmapping）。我提到我以前在这门课中教授专利数据分析（Patent Data Analytics），但分析专利以寻找研发的“空白领域”是一个极其广阔的知识海洋，以至于我实际上把它剥离出来，作为本学期提供的一门完全独立的课程。如果你对预见很认真，这两门课是相辅相成的。因为后半部分分析性很强，并且使用开源软件和Excel，我将通过预先录制的视频提供核心的操作步骤。这使得班上的数据专家可以快速浏览，而初学者可以暂停并按照自己的节奏一步步地操作。我们计划了几次客座讲座，包括下周的Seng Meng和第五周来自法国的Renee。在漫长的农历新年假期之后，我将讲解知识管理。我最初计划去旅行，但决定留下来并讲完这些材料，因为班级规模庞大，意味着我们极度需要整整两周的时间来进行期末展示。

    关于那些期末小组项目：你们有两个选择。更好的选择是一个开放式的项目，在这个项目中你们分析一家真实公司的实际情报活动——例如，描绘SP集团如何主导国家能源情报，或者一家特定的初创公司如何在其领域内航行。如果你缺乏行业人脉或工作经验，你可以使用Canvas中提供的备用选项：关于“士卓曼（Straumann）”（一家瑞士中小企业）的案例研究。让我非常坦白地说：那些努力在一家真实公司上做开放式项目的小组，绝对会比那些仅仅展示预先包装好的士卓曼案例的小组得分更高。对于那些零经验的人来说，士卓曼仅仅是一个基本要求；如果你们想拿高分，就去做开放式的项目。

  - [20:07:27 - 20:12:42] **Finalizing Logbook Logistics and Forum Format**

    Addressing a question about the logbook format: There is no rigid template. You simply choose five topics from the semester. As discussed, a Level 1 entry just summarizes the academic theory (e.g., summarizing Carlson's article). A Level 2 entry connects that theory to your workplace (e.g., detailing a workshop your company ran). A Level 3 entry requires deep critical thinking, reflecting on the specific failures or problems encountered during that workplace activity and theorizing how it could have been fixed. You can focus your five entries entirely on the later, data-heavy analytical tools if you prefer. You can also email me your drafts mid-semester for feedback before final submission.

    Finally, regarding the forums: To accommodate the split between AI-users and experience-based learners, I will not use the clunky Canvas discussion board. Instead, I will create dedicated Google Docs. One document will be strictly for those using ChatGPT, and a separate document will be for those relying purely on personal experience. Please ensure you put your actual registered name and matriculation number on your entries so I can accurately grade you—no nicknames. Feel free to use creative formats like mind maps instead of writing essays. There is no fixed format; I am just looking for creativity and genuine knowledge sharing. I strictly warned the ChatGPT users not to pollute the experience-based document, or I will penalize them. After taking a quick class vote, we agreed to hold these forum challenges only every *alternate* week to avoid overwhelming you, and I will phase them out entirely by Week 8 or 9 so you can focus entirely on your group projects. That is all for today! For next week, please thoroughly read the Foresight Benchmarking Report, as your next "Challenge of the Day"—which carries high weightage—will be drawn directly from it. See you next week!

    解答关于日志格式的问题：没有僵化的模板。你只需从本学期中选择五个主题。正如所讨论的，第一级条目只是总结学术理论（例如，总结Carlson的文章）。第二级条目将该理论与你的工作场所联系起来（例如，详细描述你公司举办的一次研讨会）。第三级条目需要深度的批判性思维，反思在该工作场所活动中遇到的具体失败或问题，并从理论上探讨本可以如何解决。如果你愿意，你可以将你的五个条目完全集中在后期的、侧重数据分析的工具上。你也可以在学期中通过电子邮件将你的草稿发给我，以便在最终提交前获得反馈。

    最后，关于论坛：为了适应AI用户和基于经验的学习者之间的划分，我不会使用笨重的Canvas讨论板。相反，我将创建专门的Google Docs。一份文档将严格供那些使用ChatGPT的人使用，另一份独立的文档将供那些完全依赖个人经验的人使用。请确保在你的条目上写上你实际注册的姓名和学号，这样我才能准确地给你打分——不要用昵称。可以随意使用思维导图等创造性格式，而不是写长篇大论。没有固定的格式；我只是在寻找创造力和真正的知识分享。我严厉警告ChatGPT用户不要污染基于经验的文档，否则我会惩罚他们。在进行快速的课堂投票后，我们同意只在*每隔*一周举行这些论坛挑战，以避免给你们带来太大压力，我会在第8或第9周彻底取消它们，以便你们可以完全专注于小组项目。今天就到这里！下周，请仔细阅读《预见基准报告》（Foresight Benchmarking Report），因为你们的下一个“今日挑战”——权重很高——将直接从中提取。下周见！
## Week 2
  - [18:00:00 - 18:01:26] **Class Administration and Registration Issues**

    For those of you who are here but haven't officially registered for the module, I need to ask you to please look for a different class. After our first lesson, I received an overwhelming number of emails from students asking to register for this module. We are simply not allowing anybody else in unless this module is a strict requirement for their specific area of specialization. So, if you are sitting here without having successfully registered, please go and find a better class for this semester. I apologize for being strict, but I had to decline many emails. I was actually hoping the class numbers would drop; they did initially, and I was happy about that. But then the numbers increased again because many different specializations came in. I don't know if some of you went around telling people that the workload for this class is light or something similar, but whatever the reason, there were just too many emails. I eventually had to stop replying altogether and firmly state that the module is closed. I apologize for that. Looking around, I see two new faces today. Have you both successfully registered for the module? Which program are you from? Energy Systems? Great. Is there anyone else who is new and didn't attend last week's class? Okay, let's get going and cover some ground before Seng Meng arrives.

    对于那些坐在这里但还没有正式注册这门课的同学，请你们去寻找其他的课程。在第一节课之后，我收到了大量的邮件，都是要求注册这门课的。我们不能再接受任何学生了，除非这门课是他们专业方向的必修课。所以，如果你没有成功注册而坐在这里，请为这学期另外找一门更合适的课。很抱歉我必须这么严格，因为我已经拒绝了很多邮件。我本来希望选课人数能降下来；一开始确实降了，我挺高兴的。但后来人数又涨了上去，因为很多其他专业的学生也来了。我不知道是不是你们当中有人出去说这门课课业负担很轻还是怎么的，不管什么原因，邮件实在太多了。到最后我不得不停止回复，并明确表示这门课已经关闭选课。对此我感到抱歉。环顾一下四周，我今天看到了两张新面孔。你们都已经成功注册了吗？你们是哪个项目的？能源系统？很好。还有其他人是新生、上周没来上课的吗？好的，在 Seng Meng 到达之前，我们先开始讲一些内容。

  - [18:01:26 - 18:05:12] **Agenda Setting and Forum Feedback**

    This is actually the first time I've added a slide at the very last minute right before class. That has never happened in my teaching history! Let's have a brief brainstorming session before our guest arrives. Welcome back, everyone. I hope you are all doing well. Interestingly, right after the first week, I had someone send in their logbook seeking feedback, which was really nice to see. Also, have you all formed your project groups yet? It's not incredibly urgent; you can take your time, talk to people around you, and then form your groups. But if you have already formed your group, please let Cheng Hong know your group name along with the members in it. We are looking at a maximum of five to six members per group. If the final class size ends up being sixty or sixty-one—unless some of you still plan to drop out, which you have some time to do—it means we will have a maximum of ten groups. This means we will need two weeks allocated for presentations towards the end of the semester. I will need to adjust the later part of the syllabus accordingly to accommodate those weeks. Today's agenda is quite packed. How many of you went through the Corporate Foresight Benchmarking Report for this week? Are you ready for a challenge? We will tackle that after the guest lecture. I thought I would make it a bit different today to foster some synergy within the groups. It's going to be a group challenge today rather than an individual one. However, if the group genuinely feels there are free riders, you can let me know. Conversely, if you feel someone explored the topic in much more detail and was a key contributor, let me know that as well so they can get extra points. Our standard agenda applies: we will do a summary of last week, Seng Meng will give his talk, and then we will dive deep into foresighting. Last week we touched on what foresighting is, and today we are focusing on why it is crucial, which is exactly what the benchmarking report illustrates. Are there any questions from last week regarding what foresighting is or regarding Carlson's article? I noticed there were quite a few organic, non-ChatGPT discussion threads on the forum, which is excellent. I prefer seeing genuine thoughts over AI-generated ones. There was one random, strangely generated post on the ChatGPT thread; I couldn't figure out who posted it, but it was very weird. Overall, good job. The total number of forum posts has come down, which is manageable and nice. I am not going to open any new post topics for this week, so the current discussion will continue until next week. Please do continue contributing. Any questions on Carlson's article? Yes, Ada? You mentioned returning to Canvas because it's difficult to post visual content like mind maps on the current forum platform. I understand; I didn't set up the current system to easily accommodate figures. Can you post those diagrams directly on Canvas? If there is a block diagram or a mind map, please post it there. That's excellent feedback, thank you. Going forward, I'll return to using the Canvas forum for both the ChatGPT and non-ChatGPT discussions. If anyone has any other difficulties with the module's logistics, please feel free to let me know early on. There is no point in complaining at the very end of the semester; it's worthless by then. Raise your concerns beforehand. Now, let's answer a few recap questions.
